  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5340c5ac-02b8-4ed0-8a3f-0fe2cf893e57'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16322493226695420060">Twelve-year-old Sophie Foster has a secret. She’s a Telepath—someone who hears the thoughts of everyone around her. It’s a talent she’s never known how to explain.<br/><br/>Everything changes the day she meets Fitz, a mysterious boy who appears out of nowhere and also reads minds. She discovers there’s a place she does belong, and that staying with her family will place her in grave</span>
  <span id="freeText16322493226695420060" style="display:none">Twelve-year-old Sophie Foster has a secret. She’s a Telepath—someone who hears the thoughts of everyone around her. It’s a talent she’s never known how to explain.<br /><br />Everything changes the day she meets Fitz, a mysterious boy who appears out of nowhere and also reads minds. She discovers there’s a place she does belong, and that staying with her family will place her in grave danger. In the blink of an eye, Sophie is forced to leave behind everything and start a new life in a place that is vastly different from anything she has ever known.<br /><br />Sophie has new rules to learn and new skills to master, and not everyone is thrilled that she has come “home.” <br />There are secrets buried deep in Sophie’s memory—secrets about who she really is and why she was hidden among humans—that other people desperately want. Would even kill for.<br /><br />In this page-turning debut, Shannon Messenger creates a riveting story where one girl must figure out why she is the key to her brand-new world, before the wrong person finds the answer first.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16322493226695420060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

I just can't get over how horrible Fitz acted toward Sophie in Exile to want Fitzfie, and Dex is better at being a friend than a romantic partner. Keefe is funny, kind, and respectful toward Sophie throughout the series, which makes him best suited for being her boyfriend.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/36361783-brittany-quarters"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1414470805i/36361783._UX100_CR0,23,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/36361783-brittany-quarters">Brittany Quarters</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This book is great. I'm fifteen, and I read it with an open mind. I didn't focus on the writing or the characters, I read it just to have fun.<br/>I own al<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This book is great. I'm fifteen, and I read it with an open mind. I didn't focus on the writing or the characters, I read it just to have fun.<br />I own all of them so far and have loaned them to all my friends, who also loved them.<br /><br />And, keep in mind, this is a book written for middle graders. Not teens. It wasn't written for people used to YA books with more complex themes.<br /><br />This is a book to laugh at and have fun with, I highly recommend it.<br /><br />And don't be a Rotten Egg, it wasn't for us older readers anyway. :)<br /><br />Who recommended it to you? Do they own the book? If so, you could just ask to borrow it or look at it. And, you can start reading the beginning on Amazon.<br />I hope you do read it. :)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_430107374" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/430107374" />
    <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers"><img alt="TheBookSmugglers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316717753p2/1223249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/430107374?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheBookSmugglers" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers">TheBookSmugglers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1223249-thebooksmugglers?shelf=terrible-books">terrible-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1223249-thebooksmugglers?shelf=mg">mg</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer430107374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17842032381450709887">Original review posted on <a href='https://www.goodreads.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Book Smugglers</a><br/><br/><b>Thea’s Take:</b><br/><br/>There are two ends of the CG animated movie spectrum. On the one side, there are gems like Wall-E and Up and Toy Story. On the other, there are the lamentable films like Fly Me to the Moon, or Robots, or Shark Tale. Granted, many kids like all of these films and there is some entertainment value to find in each of them – but there’s a huge difference in storytelling skill and in quality.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, Keeper of the Lost Cities falls deep on</span>
  <span id="freeText17842032381450709887" style="display:none">Original review posted on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Smugglers</a><br /><br /><b>Thea’s Take:</b><br /><br />There are two ends of the CG animated movie spectrum. On the one side, there are gems like Wall-E and Up and Toy Story. On the other, there are the lamentable films like Fly Me to the Moon, or Robots, or Shark Tale. Granted, many kids like all of these films and there is some entertainment value to find in each of them – but there’s a huge difference in storytelling skill and in quality.<br /><br />Unfortunately, Keeper of the Lost Cities falls deep on the Shark Tale end of the MG/YA spectrum. A poor man’s Harry Potter, featuring a super special snowflake of a heroine, Keeper of the Lost Cities is a sadly disappointing – and frequently laughable – dud.<br /><br />But let’s start at the beginning, shall we? From the synopsis, this novel seems like it would be about a telepathic twelve year old girl that discovers secrets about her family, her true birthright, and her abilities. Right? What Keeper of the Lost Cities delivers instead is a story about ultra-beautiful, ultra-intelligent, ultra-magical elves (yes, elves), whose existence is secret from disgusting humans. It then morphs into Harry Potter knock-off land, complete with a prestigious, secret and ultra selective academy for young prodigious elves, with classes in specialized areas like alchemy and telepathy. Oh yeah, and it turns out that Sophie Foster, our protagonist, is not only superduper desirable (a humble twelve year old, but already commanding the attentions of fifteen year olds) but possesses unparalleled power and is The One who can Save them All.<br /><br />I could go on and on, so let me just focus on the three areas that bothered me the most regarding Keeper of the Lost Cities: the blase treatment/combo of science and magic, Sophie’s super specialness (and unconvincing nature as a character), and the unabashed Harry Potter ripoffs.<br /><br />Let’s start with Science and Magic. When it’s done well, I love a speculative fiction book that blends fantasy elements with sci fi, magic with hard science. This is, I suspect, what Shannon Messenger attempted to accomplish in this novel. Unfortunately, it just doesn’t work. From very early on in the book, we learn that even “the slowest elf can still trump a human” – and that elves, apparently, know ALL the things about genetics and DNA and relative physics, but say this isn’t science OR magic. As heartthrob elf Fitz tells our heroine Sophie:<br /><br /> <blockquote>“This is…magic?”<br /><br /> Fitz laughed – a full body laugh, like it was the funniest thing he’d ever heard [...] “No,” he said when he’d regained control. “Magic is a stupid idea humans came up with to try to explain things they couldn’t understand.”</blockquote><br /><br />But in the next breath, when Fitz starts to describe the impossible apparating speed-of-light travel, he tells Sophie that elves “light leap”:<br /><br /> <blockquote>He held the pathfinder up to the sun, casting a ray of light onto his hand. “Light leaping. We hitched a ride on a beam of light that was headed straight here.”<br /><br /> “That’s impossible [...] You need infinite energy for light travel. Haven’t you heard of the theory of relativity?”<br /><br /> She thought she had him stumped with that one, but he just laughed again. “That’s the dumbest thing I’ve ever heard.”</blockquote><br /><br />No further explanation, until a few pages later, when Fitz tells Sophie:<br /><br /> <blockquote>This is how the world really works. It’s not magic. It’s just how it is.</blockquote><br /><br />Well THAT explains everything, then. In this type of setting, magic would be completely acceptable as an explanation for feathered dinosaur pets, catching lightning in a bottle, using elderberries to transmutate iron, and so on. But instead, Keeper of the Lost Cities insists on not-science science, not-magic magic, and the end result is, well, ridiculous.<br /><br />Which brings me to my next gripe: Sophie, the Special Snowflake. When we first meet Sophie, we learn that she is twelve years old, telepathic, possessing a photographic memory, and a high school senior that has been accepted at Yale University. We also learn that she is ‘the prettiest girl in school’, that she is an unprecedentedly powerful telepath, sickeningly sweet and good, and everyone rushes to her aid at slightest provocation. And I just want to include this quote, because Ana and I both had a good laugh when we read it:<br /><br /> <blockquote>Her family couldn’t be her family.<br /><br /> She took a deep breath and let the reality settle in.<br /><br /> The strange thing was, in some ways it made sense. It explained why she always felt so out of place around them – the slender blonde among her chubby brunette family.</blockquote><br /><br />Oh WOE! WOE! The life of a slender blonde in a chubby brunette family.<br /><br />And then, finally, there’s the big whopping Harry Potter Ripoff problem. I’ll make this easy: as soon as Sophie gets to Elfland, she hears that she has been invited to attend a prestigious academy for aspiring young <s>witches and wizards</s> elves called <s>Hogwarts</s> Foxfire. The school is presided over by a benevolent headmaster <s>Dumbledore</s> Dame Alina, who also gets to pick the constantly changing <s>sweet treat password</s> sweet treat tasting flavor that unlocks every student’s locker (on day one, the flavor is <s>Fizzing Whizbees</s> Mallowmelt). <s>Harry</s> Sophie quickly makes friends with <s>Hermione and Ron</s> Marella and Dex, and Dex happens to be a <s>mudblood bad</s> match byproduct, meaning that his parents were <s>muggles</s> non-noble elves. While at school, Sophie excels and is a natural at almost all of her subjects, except for <s>potions</s> alchemy (<s>Professor Snape</s> Lady Galvin seems to really have it out for Sophie for some reason).<br /><br />And on and on the list goes. I’ll stop here, though. While I’m certain there are many people out there that will enjoy Keeper of the Lost Cities, this book failed to work for me on any level.<br /><br /><b>Ana’s Take:</b><br /><br />Yes, to all that. Thea covered basically everything I wanted to say and I don’t have a lot more to add but here is my two cents. Keeper of the Lost Cities is a ridiculous book and I wish I could just make fun of it, disregard it simply as a bad book experience and think no more of it. But this is such a blatant, poor imitation of Harry Potter with the addition of extremely uncomfortable Racefail that I must look at it from a serious perspective.<br /><br />I do not have anything to add to Thea’s assessment of Sophie but I have a couple of things to add to her other areas of concern – the Magic x Science conundrum and the Harry Potter Ripoffs.<br /><br />With regards to the former, my main problem with the ridiculous not-science science and not-magic magic is that it results in a complete lack of internal logic and that is a way too big a flaw in the very construction of the story. The idea that the elves don’t know a lot about the human world is reinforced throughout the story – elves often wonder what a “dollar” is or what is “France”. They also insist that what they do is not science. And yet the very human scientific concept of “DNA” and genetics research is at the very centre of this story.<br /><br />Regarding the clear Harry Potter Ripoff, I can add a lot more to Thea’s breakdown:<br /><br />All <s>wizards</s> elves <s>perform spells</s> have gifts and <s>Harry</s> Sophie soon learns that there are three <s>Unforgivable Curses</s> gifts that are frowned upon: <s>the deadly Killing Curse, the Cruciatus Curse and the Imperius Curse</s> the deadly Pyrokineticsm, Infliction and Mermerizing. She also learns to play the <s>wizard’s</s> elven game of <s>Quidditch</s> Catch and that there are other people who don’t really like her like the snobby <s>Lucius</s> Cassius.<br /><br />I wish I was kidding.<br /><br />And that brings me to my last point – the brown-skinned Gnomes who work for the Elves as their gardeners.<br /><br />This is a world in which the vast majority of elves are described as impossibly beautiful with fair skin (there is the odd “olive” skinned elf) and shiny blue/teal eyes. And where, even though everybody works, they do so because they want to because elves are rich and don’t really need money. But basically the elves have important jobs but the Gnomes tend their gardens. And those are the only creatures within the novel described as “brown-skinned”. Then Sophia asks those Gnomes are servants and is promptly told off because of course the elves do not keep servants. The gnomes CHOOSE to live with the elves for their own protection and help them with their gardens because they enjoy it.<br /><br />The obliviousness to the real-life, historical and racial implication of this point is completely mind-blowing and what made me enraged rather than potentially amused by the book.<br /><br />In fairness, it is very possible that this might be addressed at some point in the series (after all, didn’t Hermione Granger address the problem of the House-Elves in the Harry Potter series?) and some readers will probably not care about the similarities to HP or even appreciate it as homage of sorts – I am not one of them. Finding the similarities between this and the Harry Potter books might actually have been fun if it wasn’t so awkward – plus the characterisation here is nowhere near as good as Rowling’s endearing creations and this means that characters here are flat, thin, poorly constructed imitations.<br /><br />Ultimately this is what it boils down to: Keeper of the Lost Cities is not one of the worst books I have ever read but it is certainly one of the most laughable ones. And it made me despair that books like these even get to see the light of day. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17842032381450709887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer350845869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5249964371435744136">🌟Ridiculously good! I love it. And I imagine I would have been even more head-over-the-heels, had I gotten this one to read as a kid. Still, even for an adult, this is an immensely entertaining read. Complete with a new world, tidy loose endings wrapped up, likable protagonists, Harry-Potteresque schools... And Telepaths, Mesmers, Inflicters, Washers, Descryers, Atlantis, Exilium, Eternalia, Foxfire, prodigies, talent-based nobility, Dames and Sirs, society that had no death (almost!), Slurps an</span>
  <span id="freeText5249964371435744136" style="display:none">🌟Ridiculously good! I love it. And I imagine I would have been even more head-over-the-heels, had I gotten this one to read as a kid. Still, even for an adult, this is an immensely entertaining read. Complete with a new world, tidy loose endings wrapped up, likable protagonists, Harry-Potteresque schools... And Telepaths, Mesmers, Inflicters, Washers, Descryers, Atlantis, Exilium, Eternalia, Foxfire, prodigies, talent-based nobility, Dames and Sirs, society that had no death (almost!), Slurps and Burps (!), Moonlarks or suldreen), meganeuras, dwarves and knomes, and, of course, elves... Gosh!<br /><br />There are some influences and analogues <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_influences_and_analogues">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_P...</a> and I love it. Duh! I loved HP books and a lot of the other analogues that could be traced and I'm positively enamoured with the KLC series. <br /><br />Q:<br />“You’re saying I’m . . . an alien?” <br />… Fitz erupted into laugher. … <br />“I’m saying you’re an elf.” (c)<br />Q: <br />They weren’t exactly fans of their resident child prodigy. They called her Curvebuster. (c)<br />Q:<br />Garwin was still bitter Yale had offered her a full scholarship. His rejection letter had arrived a few weeks before. <br />Not that Sophie was allowed to go. (c)<br />Q:<br />“Is that your magic wand?” she couldn’t resist asking.<br />He rolled his eyes. “Actually, it’s a pathfinder.” (c)<br />Q:<br />Places this beautiful weren’t supposed to exist, much less appear out of thin air. (c)<br />Q:<br />It was so quiet there, just the gentle breeze brushing her face and the soft murmur of the river. No traffic, no chatter, no hammering, unspoken thoughts. She could get very used to the silence. But it felt strange, too. Like something was missing. (c)<br />Q:<br />“Laws are rarely broken.”<br />Well, that was different. Humans broke the law all the time. (c)<br />Q:<br />… Haven’t you heard of the theory of relativity?” … <br />“That’s the dumbest thing I’ve ever heard. Who came up with that?” (c)<br />Q:<br />“Humans do the best they can—but their minds can’t begin to comprehend the complexities of reality.” (c)<br />Q:<br />Other babies learned to walk. You learned to pace. (c)<br />Q:<br />“How long do elves live?” ...<br />“We don’t know,”… “No one’s died of old age yet.” (c)<br />Q:<br />“You seriously expect me to jump?” <br />“I can push you if you’d prefer.” (c)<br />Q:<br />Humans are always doing crazy, dangerous things. If they’re not lighting something on fire, they’re spilling oil in the ocean or blowing something up. (c)<br />Q:<br />“You can see my cells?”<br />“Of course. Did you think I was wearing these glasses because they make me look dashing?” (c)<br />Q:<br />Grady and Edaline train the animals to be vegetarians by feeding them gnomish produce; that way they won’t hunt one another once they’re moved to the Sanctuary.”<br />Another roar interrupted their conversation. Whatever it was sounded like it wasn’t happy about its new diet plan. (c)<br />Q:<br />Sophie cringed, hoping she wasn’t about to watch her new guardian become lizard food. (c)<br />Q:<br />“A gnome ran in during breakfast and yelled something about a manticore stinging a stegosaurus, and they both ran off.” <br />“And people say my parents are weird.” (c)<br />Q:<br />If she was good for them, maybe they’d want to keep her. (c)<br />Q:<br />“If you weren’t so obviously alive, I would assume I was probing a dead mind.” (c)<br />Q:<br />“Don’t mind Bullhorn,” Elwin said as Sophie backed against the door. “He’s harmless.”<br />Bullhorn looked like a demented ferret with beady purple eyes. “What is he?”<br />“A banshee. Adorable, isn’t he?” (c)<br />Q:<br />Lady Anwen told her in multispeciesial studies that she hadn’t laughed so hard in 324 years. (c)<br />Q:<br />“Your concentration controls how you use the energy—where you send it, how much you send. But the actual energy and strength comes from your core. Don’t you feel the pull in your gut when you draw on it?” (с)<br />Q:<br />Potential is nothing if it’s never lived up to, now is it? (c)<br />Q:<br />Dex had been nagging her for months to try an elixir he invented called Nogginease, which contained limbium, a rare mineral that could supposedly clear her mind. She’d resisted, since she couldn’t use it during the exams, but maybe it was like learning to ride a bike. She needed training wheels to start. (c)<br />Q:<br />It was hard to resist the urge to crawl under a rock and disappear for a decade or two. (c)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10534540725495401639">ALL KINDS OF AWESOME. Seriously am in love with this book/series and its characters. <br/><br/>KEEPER OF THE LOST CITIES is a fantasy mystery of epic proportions--and it's captivating from page one.<br/><br/>While it's perfectly fitted for middle grade readers (even reluctant readers will burn through this and beg for more!) I have to be honest and say that I don't read very much middle grade. But I'm 31, and this book is still one of my all-time favorites. The reach of KEEPER OF THE LOST CITIES extends from those </span>
  <span id="freeText10534540725495401639" style="display:none">ALL KINDS OF AWESOME. Seriously am in love with this book/series and its characters. <br /><br />KEEPER OF THE LOST CITIES is a fantasy mystery of epic proportions--and it's captivating from page one.<br /><br />While it's perfectly fitted for middle grade readers (even reluctant readers will burn through this and beg for more!) I have to be honest and say that I don't read very much middle grade. But I'm 31, and this book is still one of my all-time favorites. The reach of KEEPER OF THE LOST CITIES extends from those middle grade readers all the way to adults of any age. Try it, you'll see what I mean.<br /><br />The characters are each fully developed and completely lovable--even (especially) the troublemakers. The pages are full of intrigue and twists and mystery--all while Sophie Foster (the main character) struggles to find her place in her new world. The setting is lush, the creatures are awesome--and just as lovable as the characters, and the bad guys are pretty freaking scary.<br /><br />If you only read one book for the rest of the year, MAKE IT THIS ONE!!! You'll be thanking me after.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/380009292?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison" href="/user/show/11402263-allison">Allison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer380009292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13413752816613636608">Alright, I will start this off by saying that this book was written by my little sister....and for you to fully understand what this means I must explain a few things to you. Shannon has always been the over achiever in the family, she's younger than me, yet managed to graduate a couple days before me, 4.0 and valedictorian no less! She graduated college, which I never even went to, and she always manages to do things like change the lightbulbs, wear accessories and eyeliner, and bring a jacket </span>
  <span id="freeText13413752816613636608" style="display:none">Alright, I will start this off by saying that this book was written by my little sister....and for you to fully understand what this means I must explain a few things to you. Shannon has always been the over achiever in the family, she's younger than me, yet managed to graduate a couple days before me, 4.0 and valedictorian no less! She graduated college, which I never even went to, and she always manages to do things like change the lightbulbs, wear accessories and eyeliner, and bring a jacket (whereas I am hopeless in all these departments!=)) So when Shannon FINALLY let me read her book, I knew it would be good.....There was a tiny part of me though that didn't want to like it.....because...COME ON, she can't really be good at everything can she?? Well any hope I had of not liking it was gone by around page 50.....I was hooked, so hooked in fact that my noisy animals distracting me from my reading proved to be too much! So I got in my car and drove to the beach and spent all day sitting on the sand until I finished all 400 plus pages of it. It was good, really good. I won't go into the story, because it's hard to explain it, but it is really genuinely beautiful. It's witty and sharp and obviously extremely engrossing. The world that my sister has created here is pretty much, for lack of a better word (see I told you she is the smart one!) awesome. I can see why there is so much buzz building up for the release of this one! So all I have to say to everyone else is that you should pick up a copy just as soon as you can.....and to Shannon I can only tip my imaginary hat (I'm not nearly good enough with accessories to have a real hat!) and say good job little sister, you are clearly going to be a big success! <br />PS....remember the little people when you do become a success.....Like when you are doing casting for the male actors in the movie that will undoubtably be made from this.....remember me....and my excellent spectating skills!=)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13413752816613636608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7112837812279437757"><b>Rating:</b> Though I nearly DNFed in the beginning (they're ELVES?! She's HARRY FREAKING POTTER?! THEY'RE <i>ELVES?!?!</i>), ultimately I was charmed by this middle grade fantasy.<br/><br/><b>The cover:</b> 99% of the reason I wanted this. LOOOOK at it! Normal-but-not-normal preteen girl suddenly discovers she is part of a magical world she nev</span>
  <span id="freeText7112837812279437757" style="display:none"><b>Rating:</b> Though I nearly DNFed in the beginning (they're ELVES?! She's HARRY FREAKING POTTER?! THEY'RE <i>ELVES?!?!</i>), ultimately I was charmed by this middle grade fantasy.<br><br><b>The cover:</b> 99% of the reason I wanted this. LOOOOK at it! And at Sophie's oh-so-glorious middle grade hair. Let's pretend I looked like that at age 12.<br><br><b>The story:</b> I came so close to giving up on this one. I thought the beginning was a MESS. Normal-but-not-normal preteen girl suddenly discovers she is part of a magical world she never knew existed. Yeah, we've all read it before, but it's possible to pull this conceit off in a pretty original matter. Instead, for most of the beginning, I was rolling my eyes and saying, "Harry Potter. Ooh, that was Twilight-esque. OH MY GOD, THEY ARE *NOT* GOING TO A MAGICAL SHOPPING STREET AND INTO A MAGICAL POTIONS STORE CALLED <i>SLURPS AND BURPS.</i>"<br><br>Sophie is your average twelve-year-old high school senior who can read minds (bwahahahahaha). One day, on a school field trip, a hot fourteen-year-old boy comes up and tells her she doesn't belong in the human world. Sophie begs and begs to know why, and eventually Fitz, hottie extraordinaire despite the fact that he is named Fitz, tells her: she is an elf.<br><br>

        <img height="200" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380429848ra/861467.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
      
    
    <br>
    
      Nope...
    
    <br>
  
<br><br>
  
    <br>
    
      
        <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380429848i/861468.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
      
    
    <br>
    
      Not quite...
    
    <br>
  
<br><br>
  
    <br>
    
      
        <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380429848ra/861469.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
      
    
    <br>
    
      YEP THAT'S THE ONE
    
    <br>
  
<br><br>I don't know why I snickered every time the world "elf" was on the page, but I did. It was so silly. Anyway, the world-building from this point on isn't bad, though it is, again, a little silly. The elves sequestered themselves away from the doomed, dirty humans a couple thousand years ago, retreating into the "lost" cities of Atlantis, Shangri-La, etcetera. Elves kind of suck for this. Anyway, Fitz shows up to find Sophie in the human world, and he's all:<br><br><img height="223" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380429848ra/861470.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Because it turns out Sophie is <i>the specialest little snowflake that you ever did see</i>. Anything an elf can do, Sophie can do better. No, best. Sophie can do it backwards and upside down and with her eyes closed and when she was a fetus. It was quite exahausting to spend the whole beginning of the book discovering all ninety-thousand of Sophie's mystical gifts. "No elf in a thousand years has had THAT ability! No elf has ever had BROWN eyes! No elf has EVER made me want to commit suicide before!"<br><br>
  
    <br>
    
      
        <img alt="image" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380429848ra/861471.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
      
    
    <br>
    
      Oops, I angered the pretty.
    
    <br>
  
<br><br>Aw, I kid, Legolas, really. It wasn't that bad. I was just feeling grumpy, and the book wasn't working for me. We spend a LOT of time establishing the world and Sophie's awesomeness. Messenger actually broke my heart when Sophie had to say goodbye to her human family forever... but then she skips right past it, and Sophie, while thinking of her family every now and then, never feels that pain again. <br><br>But then, things get better. Things pick up once Sophie finds a tentative, surrogate family, makes it past the Wizengamot elf council (which features one council memeber whose entire life mission is, inexplicably, to get Sophie exiled) and goes off to elfing school.<br><br>
  
    <br>
    
      
        <img height="320" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380429848ra/861472.gif" width="151" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
      
    
    <br>
    
      "Elfing school? REALLY?"
    
    <br>
  
<br><br>Yeah. Really, Legolas. But still, this is the point where the book gains a really delightful sense of humor. Sophie becomes less of an assortment of cool abilities and more of a sweet, earnest person, desperate to fit in somewhere and desperate to have a family. The friends she makes are what really sold the book for me. Dex the best friend is absolutely wonderful, even if he is one of 654323 male characters in love with Sophie. Keefe, who could be a Weasley triplet, is hilarious, and Fitz is pretty swoony for a pre-pubescent elf.<br><br>
  
    <br>
    
      
        <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/677710.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
      
    
    <br>
    
      "DAMN STRAIGHT. WE ELVES BE FINE"
    
    <br>
  
<br><br>Never doubted it for a second, Legolas. And even though some Harry Potter parallels remain (oh, so you're known for getting sent to the hospital wing a lot, are you, Sophie?), the book becomes its own by the time big things are going down. All lot of the magical world-building feels dense  and original and plausible. You learn WHY Sophie is the best elf in the history of elves, and it actually makes sense. There was a twist I didn't see coming at all. And the mystery is pretty engrossing.<br><br>Mostly, this book overcame it's rocky start by winning my heart (that sounds like a country song). Everything in the latter half of the book was completely adorable. Sophie gets a cute little animal sidekick, bonds with the bitchy mean girl, and has a couple really sad moments with her foster parents. Suddenly, I found myself caring. Also, jokes! This book makes funnies! I like funnies.<br><br>I really want to read the sequel so I can find out if all my inappropriate ships come to light. This book was such a bizarre journey for me, from open disgust to total adoration. HOW DID YOU DO THIS, BOOK? I DON'T UNDERSTAND THIS WITCHCRAFT ELFCRAFT. You win this one, adorable little elf-people. You win.<br><br>
  
    <br>
    
      
        <img alt="image" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380429848ra/861473.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
      
    
    <br>
    
      Stop looking so smug, you gorgeous creature.
    
    <br>
  
<br><br><b>ETA:</b> I forgot about Sophie's habit of PULLING OUT HER EYELASHES when she's nervous! Who does that? That is horrifying. That better be significant later on, because as a personality quirk, it is DISTURBING.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7112837812279437757" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2846444914" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2846444914" />
    <a title="Amy Imogene Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84702001-amy-imogene-reads"><img alt="Amy Imogene Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548082309p2/84702001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2846444914?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy Imogene Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy Imogene Reads" href="/user/show/84702001-amy-imogene-reads">Amy Imogene Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2846444914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8883232083194258375">5<br/><br/>This was so good??? I have not had a middle grade suck me in this intensely since my first time reading Harry Potter—as an actual middle grade-aged reader—so I am shook. <br/><br/><b>World:</b> ★★★★★<br/><b>Characters:</b> ★★★★★<br/><b>Pacing:</b> ★★★★<br/><b>Series potential:</b> ★★★★★<br/><br/><i>Keeper of the Lost Cities</i> is not your average middle grade read. <b>This is an immersive, well-built, and well-told tale that caters to a middle grade audience mostly due to its 12-year-old protagonist, Sophie Foster</b>. It's not overly simplified. In fact, at times it w</span>
  <span id="freeText8883232083194258375" style="display:none">5<br /><br />This was so good??? I have not had a middle grade suck me in this intensely since my first time reading Harry Potter—as an actual middle grade-aged reader—so I am shook. <br /><br /><b>World:</b> ★★★★★<br /><b>Characters:</b> ★★★★★<br /><b>Pacing:</b> ★★★★<br /><b>Series potential:</b> ★★★★★<br /><br /><i>Keeper of the Lost Cities</i> is not your average middle grade read. <b>This is an immersive, well-built, and well-told tale that caters to a middle grade audience mostly due to its 12-year-old protagonist, Sophie Foster</b>. It's not overly simplified. In fact, at times it was more emotionally poignant than some YA fantasies. How has it taken me so long to read this? <br /><br /><b>Sophie Foster is a 12-year-old girl living in California</b>. She's branded a prodigy as her photographic memory and keen intelligence keep her at the top of every testing bracket, but that's not the main reason she's special--<b>Sophie can hear the thoughts of everyone around her</b>.<br /><br /><b>One day during a classroom field trip, Sophie meets a boy who also can read minds. He says his name is Fitz, and he's been looking for her for a long time</b>. Sophie is told that her feelings of separation, of "other" amidst her family aren't her fault--Sophie is an elf, and it's time to come home. <br /><br />Playing on the now popular story line where a Chosen One is discovered in the wrong life and brought back to the fold--just think Harry Potter, I did--<b>Sophie discovers that she is a rare kind of elf</b>, and that the elven society she finds herself in does not know what to do with her. So, <b>they send her to their magical academy</b> to learn more about how to be an elf and how to harness her abilities. <br /><br />Full disclaimer, <b>I'm a sucker for a well-done Chosen One/magical school trope</b>. Harry Potter reeled me in and I've never really come back. Because of this, <b>I was primed to enjoy <i>Keeper of the Lost Cities</i>. What I didn't expect was to fall head over heels for it.</b> <br /><br /><u>
  <b>Things that were amazing:</b>
</u> The nuanced discussion of foster case and found families and the issues that spring up as a result of those complex topics, Sophie's sense of fair play, Sophie's dynamics with her schoolmates (painfully real and yet readable), the unique magic system, the GOOD dialogue (middle grade tends to grate on me due to its reading level - it's occasionally dumbed-down beyond what is necessary). <br /><br /><u>
  <b>Things that weren't amazing:</b>
</u> Absolutely nothing. If I had to pick a negative, I found the beginning a bit slower than the rest as we were stuck in an introduction loop for the elf world and lifestyle. However, that's often the case with this trope so there wasn't really a way around it.<br /><br /><b>If you enjoyed Harry Potter, Percy Jackson, or any novel filled with magical academies and Chosen Ones--or, honestly, even if you're just a fan of fantasy novels--do yourself a favor and pick up <i>Keeper of the Lost Cities</i>.</b> It's a hidden gem and can definitely handle an adult audience.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8883232083194258375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2813647695" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2813647695" />
    <a title="BrooKe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87485390-brooke"><img alt="BrooKe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583732525p2/87485390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2813647695?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BrooKe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BrooKe" href="/user/show/87485390-brooke">BrooKe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87485390-brooke?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2813647695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6110591445833091101">3.2/5 | It's like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42080479.The_School_for_Good_and_Evil__The_School_for_Good_and_Evil___1_' title='The School for Good and Evil (The School for Good and Evil, #1) by Soman Chainani' rel='nofollow noopener'>The School for Good and Evil</a>, but better.<br/><br/>Actually, it's The School for Good and Evil with some Harry Potter thrown in along with a bit of Narnia and sprinkled with elements of Percy Jackson. And you have it. But, for real, it reminded me so much of TSfGaE; it was everything good about that series and more.<br/><br/>It's also worth mentioning how drop dead <b>gorgeous</b> every single cover in this series is. It's actually shocking.<br/><br/><b>P L O T</b><br/><br/>I was afraid at the beginning because the pacing was shit</span>
  <span id="freeText6110591445833091101" style="display:none">3.2/5 | It's like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42080479.The_School_for_Good_and_Evil__The_School_for_Good_and_Evil___1_" title="The School for Good and Evil (The School for Good and Evil, #1) by Soman Chainani" rel="nofollow noopener">The School for Good and Evil</a>, but better.<br /><br />Actually, it's The School for Good and Evil with some Harry Potter thrown in along with a bit of Narnia and sprinkled with elements of Percy Jackson. And you have it. But, for real, it reminded me so much of TSfGaE; it was everything good about that series and more.<br /><br />It's also worth mentioning how drop dead <b>gorgeous</b> every single cover in this series is. It's actually shocking.<br /><br /><b>P L O T</b><br /><br />I was afraid at the beginning because the pacing was shit. It was absolutely rubbish. This quote pretty much sums it up:<br /><i>"You look confused," he observed.<br />"Well, it's like you're saying, 'Hey, Sophie, take everything you've ever learned about anything and throw it away.'"<br />"Actually, that is what I'm saying."</i><br /><br />Literally that. We plunged headfirst into a high fantasy magic land. Sophie was a human and we got basically nothing about the first eleven years of her existence, her human life. Barely anything was pre-established, it was so much in such a short span of time and everything was so in your face. It was very info-dumpy, too. I didn't like the beginning <b>at all.</b> The only thing I cared for was the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28187.The_Lightning_Thief__Percy_Jackson_and_the_Olympians___1_" title="The Lightning Thief (Percy Jackson and the Olympians, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lightning Thief</a> nostalgia because it was similar in that it was a middle-grade series that all started one faithful day during a museum field trip.<br /><br />It was way too much. But on a brighter note, it was so rushed it seemed almost immature and, while that was annoying, it was also kind of charming in a weird way? Things seemed a lot less formal than what I'm used to reading in fantasy which was refreshing, I guess. Also, I doubt this was intentional but it definitely helped me to relate to how overwhelming Sophie found everything at the start. Information and life-changing developments were dropped like <b>BANG BANG BANG!</b><br /><br />The world building was also rushed. It also grew tiresome how constantly I was reminded of how inferior earth was to the elf world. Just about every description in the fantasy realm alluded to being superior to earth in absolutely every respect. I suppose it was meant to represent an ideal world but with magic and a way to poke fun at issues such as climate change and crime and stuff. That's nice and all but can't you describe elf land (I can't remember if it was given a general name?) without mercilessly dragging earth through the mud? (I'm sorry; I'm an earth lover and I've been triggered)<br /><br /><b>Enough of my whining.</b> The pacing significantly improved from around 70 pages onward. As soon as the school setting was introduced and things were, let's say, settled, the story flowed seamlessly in a way that was both natural and gripping. The classes were super fun, the character antics and events as well, and all the while there was this air of mystery lingering that kept me interested and had me coming up with many theories. It felt like a genuine school experience with an investigating lead and a kind of distant larger threat that said lead is too young to know that much about. In that, it reminded me a lot of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3.Harry_Potter_and_the_Sorcerer_s_Stone__Harry_Potter___1_" title="Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone (Harry Potter, #1) by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone</a>.<br /><br />The magic system was <b>so cool!</b> Telepaths, Empaths, Vanishers, Conjurers, Impacters, etc. I'm certainly excited to learn more about these abilities and what they can branch out to. I'm particularly curious about Empaths.<br /><br /><br /><b>C H A R A C T E R S</b><br /><br />Okay, at first I thought our protagonist Sophie Foster would be a Mary Sue. She was a senior in high school at the age of twelve, she had photographic memory, she was extraordinarily intelligent, magical and special. Everything seemed to come so easily for her, her successes being ridiculously convenient, but things changed once she hit Foxfire. I like that she was set up to be this insanely powerful, talented and seemingly perfect girl overflowing with potential only to have her actually struggle with several classes at school. It sounds horrible but <b>I really enjoyed seeing her mess up!</b> Learning how she worked through her failures was what really made her endearing to me. She was so determined and conscientious in school despite everything else that went on in her whirlwind life. Sophie just could not catch a bloody break which makes me worry on her behalf in the next, what, five books? I don't even know how many installments this series has. Point is, she really grew on me by the end regardless of the fact that I'm still grimacing at her name thanks to a certain bitch from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42080479.The_School_for_Good_and_Evil__The_School_for_Good_and_Evil___1_" title="The School for Good and Evil (The School for Good and Evil, #1) by Soman Chainani" rel="nofollow noopener">The School for Good and Evil</a> series.<br /><br />Dex was great. He was probably the first character to show a personality in the entire book. He was always so excited about everything, he was super blunt and he was just too cute. Dex was a great friend to Sophie, too, and, while he was irrational at times, I sympathise with his loathing of 'Wonderboys'. It's a totally realistic reaction and I appreciate him for being so real.<br /><br />Keefe stole the show even if he was pretty brief. His appearances were like candy because I just ate him up. He was hilarious and never - and I mean <b>NEVER</b> - failed to make me smile - and that's not just because his name is so weird it's funny.<br /><br />Fitz was... fine. I can't say much about a character that was often present but had no presence. The stereotypical nice guy heartthrob that's just kind of there for people - characters and readers alike - to crush on. Biana, while ever so slightly more interesting than her bro Fitz, was also very brief. I think she has more potential, though.<br /><br />Whatever; it's only the first book. I'm guessing this will be a gradual thing. I got a decent understanding of most characters but never got too much. That's good because I know them but I don't know too much for them to become dry later on. (Yes, I said <i>later on.</i> I'm definitely continuing this series.)<br /><br />Especially considering this is a middle-grade series, I could really appreciate there being so many parental figures that were involved in the younger mains' lives. Alden, Elwin, Grady, Edaline, Tiergen - they were all really present and made to be unique and interesting. It's a common issue I have when authors neglect adults in their cast, depicting them as stale, worrisome and or authoritative people who think they know what's up but really don't, instead focusing all their efforts into the younger characters in order to achieve optimal quirkiness with them alone. Edaline and Grady, specifically, hooked me.<br /><br /><br /><b>R E L A T I O N S H I P S</b><br /><br />Sophie's relationship with Grady and Edaline was so sad and precious. She's helped them attempt to move on and live their lives normally and happily. In return, they act as such good parents to her even if they do face obvious indecision. They're so healthy for each other.<br /><br />Lil' twelve-year-old Sophie was in awe of how handsome fifteen-year-old Fitz was and it was kind of adorable. I should have counted how many times she got lost in his teal eyes. I kind of wish there was more to their relationship established early on. It's a childish crush on Sophie's part whilst Fitz just extends seemingly superficial kindness to her as he does with everyone else except that one mean girl at school that isn't his sister.<br /><br />To end on a great note: The Sophie-Keefe friendship is where it's at! It worked <b>SO</b> well! He'd always be teasing her and is so straightforward with her, encouraging her in his own super endearingly snarky way:<br /><br /><i>"Look, I'm not good at the serious, supportive thing-but trust me, you're going to be fine."<br />"How do you know?"<br />He grinned. "I have a feeling you can do pretty much anything you put your mind to. So stop doubting yourself and go prove me right. You know, so I can brag about it."<br />She couldn't help smiling."</i><br /><br />... ...<br /><br />A solid start. I want to know what happens next and I hear the books only get better from here!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6110591445833091101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8431274684397021202" style="display:none">WOW!!! This book was WONDERFUL!!! My favorite read of 2018. <br /><br />Where to start... <br /><br />Romance- Sophie did have crushes of boys; mentions of hugging, hand holding... nothing bad at all. <br /><br />Violence/content- Two of the main characters get kidnapped; lots of magic, feeling severely alone; mentions of being drugged (while kidnapped), etc. <br /><br />First off- Shannon Messenger is an INCREDIBLE author. I cannot wait to read more of her work. <br /><br />The world-building in this book is mesmerizing. The details and choice of words were so beautifully precise that I could SEE the images that the author created. <br /><br />The plot was amazing. It had so many plot twists and cliff-hangers. Some books that I read consist only of constant action, and therefore, the characters are lacking realness and creativity. The characters were so real, frustrating, loving, heart-wrenching... ❤️ With every word I read, the characters became more special to me. <br /><br />This book left me in a daze until I finished it, and I LOVE the characters. <br /><br />Oh! And btw- I am totally team Sophitz... 😏😏😏</span>

  <span id="freeText4342240593696837535" style="display:none">It's been a while since I've read a good MG book and I'm glad that I've started this one. This could be one of my favorite MG books given time, maybe after I've read the next few books.<br /><br />What I love about this series is diving on a whole new world of fantasy and adventures. I've been through the world of wizardry, demigods, ghost hunters, fairy tales and the like. And this series is about elves but not like the LOTR ones with pointy ears, great eyesight and hearing, and clearly not the fairy tale ones with pointy shoes. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Though if they grow old enough (like really, really old), their eyes will become pointed. But that's not the case.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />We have elves with different abilities. Telepaths, Mesmers, Inflicters, Vanishers and more! They go to a school to discover their innate power (if they do not already now). Yeah, I know that you're thinking that it's like some other MG books but that's what I like about it. I just miss reading a book series like this.</span>

<div id="review_3603773404" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3603773404" />
    <a title="Layla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/109681904-layla"><img alt="Layla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602279778p2/109681904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3603773404?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Layla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Layla" href="/user/show/109681904-layla">Layla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781442445949" href="/book/show/16088359-keeper-of-the-lost-cities">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/109681904-layla?shelf=re-read-2020">re-read-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3603773404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12455897908080688071"><b>~4 stars~</b><br/><b>
  <i>Re-read (10/23/20)</i>
</b><br/><br/>Is there anything better than revisiting a book or book series that you loved as a child? Of course my taste in books and writing has changed much since I have last read this, but I still very much enjoyed it. And I see why I it was one of my favorite series all those years ago. This has a similar vibe to Harry Potter (aka the series I used to have an unhealthy obsession with for years hahaha), so if you are a fan of that series, and looking for a middle grade I re</span>
  <span id="freeText12455897908080688071" style="display:none"><b>~4 stars~</b><br /><b>
  <i>Re-read (10/23/20)</i>
</b><br /><br />Is there anything better than revisiting a book or book series that you loved as a child? Of course my taste in books and writing has changed much since I have last read this, but I still very much enjoyed it. And I see why I it was one of my favorite series all those years ago. This has a similar vibe to Harry Potter (aka the series I used to have an unhealthy obsession with for years hahaha), so if you are a fan of that series, and looking for a middle grade I recommend this one. <br /><br />This book follows Sophie. A 12 year old that has lived her whole life amongst humans, but one day she finds out that she is an elf and that there are a lot of secrets and conspiracies revolving around her existence.<br /><br />I love so many of these characters. I think my favorite is Keefe (obviously), but there are so many others that I adore. The plot is so fun to keep up with. There is so many things to make theories about, and I was definitely hooked, even when I knew what was going to happen.<br /><br />Most of my critiques are mostly revolving around the writing and the fact that I wasn't as blown away as I was the first time, which is understandable as I have grown out of it over time (plus the series gets better as it progresses so I'm sure most of the other books will get 5 stars). My problem with the writing, isn't objective, as I enjoy Shannon Messengers writing as a whole, but rather that it is targeted to a younger audience. I have been noticing that lately, as I have reread quite a few books, that sometimes I just cringe. It's not terrible, but I feel , if I have to pause every couple of pages because something made me want to crawl under the pillow because of second hand embarrassment, that's not good. Also there was so much blushing. One of the biggest thing I hate. When there is just constant emphasis on the blushing or flushing going on. Just no. Again, didn't ruin the book, but it's worth noting.<br /><br />I'm so happy that I decided to read this books. I have book 8.5 on hold from the library, and I want to read all the previous books before I read it because in the past I would just read the new release without any refreshment of what conspired previously and find myself lost. <br /><br />This review isn't structured how I usually structure my reviews as I always try to write a list of the stuff I like and don't like but there wasn't much to talk about for this one. Overall I recommend, especially if you need a break from difficult books that require critical thinking and glasses to read the small print. One of the wonders of middle grade.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12455897908080688071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15099815930269988517" style="display:none"><i>“This is…magic?”<br><br>Fitz laughed – a full body laugh, like it was the funniest thing he’d ever heard [...] “No,” he said when he’d regained control. “Magic is a stupid idea humans came up with to try to explain things they couldn’t understand.”</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448543529ra/17157180.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This. <div id="review_3645230432" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3645230432" />
    <a title="Adela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/118717482-adela"><img alt="Adela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606188102p2/118717482.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3645230432?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adela" href="/user/show/118717482-adela">Adela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/118717482-adela?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/118717482-adela?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3645230432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9796025122715999433">I am definitely not ready to depart with this book right now. It was just so good. SO GOOD. I haven't read a middle grade that I really liked in quite a bit, so this was a surprise! <br/><br/><b>Characters</b><br/>Sophie - She was really just okay. I didn't particularly love her or hate her. I did like how she was super smart for her age and in high school. I found that pretty interesting.<br/><br/>Fitz - In the beginning he was annoying. In the end he was annoying. No character development there.<br/><br/>Dex - In the beginning, he was</span>
  <span id="freeText9796025122715999433" style="display:none">I am definitely not ready to depart with this book right now. It was just so good. SO GOOD. I haven't read a middle grade that I really liked in quite a bit, so this was a surprise! <br /><br /><b>Characters</b><br />Sophie - She was really just okay. I didn't particularly love her or hate her. I did like how she was super smart for her age and in high school. I found that pretty interesting.<br /><br />Fitz - In the beginning he was annoying. In the end he was annoying. No character development there.<br /><br />Dex - In the beginning, he was SUPER annoying. But toward the end I learned to sort of appreciate him. I dunno. He was a nice side character that I thoroughly enjoyed. <br /><br />Keefe - THE MAN OF MY DREAMS! I'm so glad that I finally get the Sokeefe ship now. I've been waiting to read this for at least six months, if not more. <br /><br /><b>Magic System</b><br />The magic in this book was extremely unique, which I adored. I loved learning about all the new magical words and how all these elves had all these different powers. It was super interesting and intriguing. I also really enjoyed the dog thingy that Elwen had. Like how when it'd curl up next to you it meant you were close to death. My type of dog. <b>Note: El has informed me that it's actually a spirit demon. Not a dog. Oops.</b><br /><br /><b>Plot</b><br />I'm kinda obsessed with the plot of middle-grade fantasies. THEY'RE JUST SO GOOD. There's always a lot of action going on when you least expect it. I like how random stuff happened that wasn't really relevant to the main plot at all. It gave me a nice break from all the stuff going on. I didn't like how fast-paced it was in the beginning and end. It started and ended way too quickly. The middle was perfect though. <br /><br /><b>Sexism?</b><br />I didn't like how Fitze, Dex, and Keefe all said something negatively about girls at some point in this book. It was totally unnecessary and it's part of the reason I docked off a star. The three of them seemed to have this very stereotypical idea of girls only giggling about girls and 'girly stuff'. <br /><br /><b>This was a buddy read with Taylor!</b><br /><br /><b>Reading Plans</b><br />-Finish The Raven Boys before I die (probably not likely)<br />-Start Archenemies tomorrow because I am way too tired to start it today (Sorry Annie!!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9796025122715999433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1195856346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1195856346" />
    <a title="Hillary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18999155-hillary"><img alt="Hillary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601752862p2/18999155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1195856346?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hillary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hillary" href="/user/show/18999155-hillary">Hillary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13635489-keeper-of-the-lost-cities">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18999155-hillary?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18999155-hillary?shelf=low-fantasy">low-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1195856346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10281301855567577083">So um,,,I have no idea why this series is well-loved. This book is a basic mix of HP and every YA that was popular at the time this was released, and it’s not good. At ALL. <br/><b>There’s a circle in my personal hell for middle grade books that think their readers stupid, and I’m shoving <i>Keeper of the Lost Cities</i> right in.</b> No regrets. <br/><br/><b>This book did a 180 for me one third in.</b> The beginning isn’t all bad, it introduces the main character, the light-leaping magic and the elven cities made of crystals. Tha</span>
  <span id="freeText10281301855567577083" style="display:none">So um,,,I have no idea why this series is well-loved. This book is a basic mix of HP and every YA that was popular at the time this was released, and it’s not good. At ALL. <br /><b>There’s a circle in my personal hell for middle grade books that think their readers stupid, and I’m shoving <i>Keeper of the Lost Cities</i> right in.</b> No regrets. <br /><br /><b>This book did a 180 for me one third in.</b> The beginning isn’t all bad, it introduces the main character, the light-leaping magic and the elven cities made of crystals. That world building kind of charmed me. Sure, the writing felt rushed and chunky from the very first page, as if descriptions and part of the narration were missing, but I was able to push that in the back of my mind and enjoy what I had. Until more things started to show up. <br /><br />First of all, as soon as Sophie sees a cute boy she immediately thinks he’s handsome, she develops an instant crush and tries to impress him. It happens with Fitz before they have even exchanged a couple of words, it happens with Keefe, it happens with others. But she denies it. On the other side, every boy at school is also in love with her and only her. She’s not like other girls. <b>The school teenagey drama was already as cliche as it could be without these stupid crushes and I would have loved it if the author had focused her energies on making a better plot and world for the book instead of putting the drama in the foreground.</b><br /><br />The plot is laughable, like many of the details of the world building after that first shiny impact. It’s all over the place and it kind of starts only near the end when you don’t care about it anymore. Plus, it was sooo convenient. <b>Meet Sophie, the most special of the special snowflakes!</b> All the unusual powers are hers, and she wants you to think she’s worried that the other elves will think her a freak because of them. Oh, cut the crap. She loves the attention and you can see that miles away. <br />She knows the right stuff at the right moment just because, she can teleport with amazing concentration no one has, she has the best telepathy talent and no one can read her mind, she has super psychokinetic powers and she’s better than elves who have studied at the school for years. She’s also modest and kind and can’t cheat at school without her self-sabotaging and telling the teacher. Oh, what a special elf she is.<br /><br />I can’t believe I didn’t even get to experience the classes at school. <b>What’s the point of a book about a kid going to a magic school if it doesn’t show what she’s studying?</b> Honestly, this was the proof I needed to confirm that the world building sits on top of a shaking ladder. <b>The author took part of the HP world and made it quirkier, but didn’t think of making rules for it to make it believable.</b> Quirkier is key word: if you want an example of what I’m talking about, the kids at school have to lick a panel next to their locker to open it because it needs their DNA. What the actual... LOL.<br /><br /><b>I’m also unsure if I should say HP was plagiarized here?</b> The author did a great job muddying the waters, and you can tell something was taken here and there, but it’s not usually noticeable. Cases in which it’s very noticeable include: <br />- the alchemy teacher (Snape), who’s the one every kid hates and the one teacher who hates Sophie because she can’t do alchemy<br />- Stina (Draco Malfoy), a girl with two goons who hates Sophie and wants her to fail at everything<br />- the different collectible pins kids get from a specific type of candy (chocolate frogs). <br /><br />I can’t deny I thought I hit jackpot with this book at the beginning. <b>My plan was to binge a good middle grade series, but I’m going to have to look somewhere else.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10281301855567577083" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
